| BUG-SM-003 | **New WO form passed negative or NaN labor hour values to the backend.** The labor hours field had `min="0"` on the HTML `<input>` (which browsers can bypass) but `handleSubmit` used raw `parseFloat(estimatedLaborHours)` — so "abc" → `NaN`, "-5" → `-5` could be submitted. The backend would receive invalid values. | `app/(app)/work-orders/new/page.tsx` | Changed the value to `Math.max(0, parseFloat(estimatedLaborHours) \|\| 0) \|\| undefined` — coerces NaN to 0, clamps negatives to 0, then converts 0 back to `undefined` (treated as "no override"). | Shop manager accidentally types "-10" or "1hr" in the labor hours field. Backend receives invalid value. Now safely sanitized client-side before submission. |
| BUG-SM-004 | **Reports page silently showed no data when either date input was cleared, with no error message.** If `dateFrom` or `dateTo` was cleared to an empty string, `new Date("").getTime()` returns `NaN`. All timestamp comparisons with NaN return `false`, so all data was filtered out with no charts, no table rows, and no indication of why. The existing `dateRangeInvalid` error only triggered when both dates were present but inverted. | `app/(app)/reports/page.tsx` | Added `dateInputMissing` check (`!dateFrom \|\| !dateTo`). Added an amber warning banner when either date is missing. Fixed `fromTs`/`toTs` to only call `new Date()` when the date string is non-empty. | Shop manager clears the "From" date field to type a new one, tabs to something else before finishing. Charts go blank. No error. Manager assumes no revenue data for the period and escalates to billing. Now shows: "Both a From and To date are required to display report data." |

Both fields now reset to clean state each time the dialog opens. | Tech fails a sign attempt (wrong PIN), closes dialog, opens it again for a different step. | BUG-LT-HUNT-002 | **`MarkNaDialog`: `reason` text and `error` banner not cleared on re-open.** No `useEffect` existed to clear state when the dialog opened. If a tech opened the N/A dialog for Step 3, typed a reason, then closed without submitting, then opened it for Step 5, Step 5's dialog pre-filled with Step 3's reason text. Similarly, a stale error from a failed N/A attempt persisted on re-open. This is a maintenance records integrity risk: the N/A reason is a permanent record under 14 CFR 43.9(a)(2) — a tech might not notice the pre-filled wrong reason and submit it for the wrong step. | `app/(app)/work-orders/[id]/tasks/[cardId]/_components/MarkNaDialog.tsx` | Added `import { useState, useEffect }` and a `useEffect(() => { if (open) { setReason(""); setError(null); } }, [open])`. Also added `useEffect` import. Both fields now reset each time the dialog opens. | Tech opens N/A dialog for Step 3 ("Aircraft does not have oxygen system"), types reason, decides to cancel. Then opens N/A dialog for Step 7. Step 7's dialog shows Step 3's reason pre-filled. Tech doesn't notice, clicks "Mark N/A". Step 7 now has the wrong reason in the permanent maintenance record. Now: fresh dialog every time. |
| BUG-PC-009 | **Loaners return dialog did not reset `returnForm` state on close.** The `onOpenChange` handler only called `setReturnDialogId(null)` — it never cleared `returnForm`. `returnForm` was only reset inside `handleReturn` on successful submission (line 195). If a clerk opened the return dialog, typed condition notes, then dismissed via X or "Cancel", those notes persisted. Opening the return dialog for the next item would show the previous item's condition notes pre-filled. Clerk doesn't notice, submits. Wrong condition note is permanently recorded for the second unit. Now: fresh form every time. |

A parts clerk who lands on this page from the inventory list (`/parts → + Add Part`) has no way to cancel back to inventory. Clicking "Cancel" drops them on the parts receiving queue instead of where they came from. | `app/(app)/parts/new/page.tsx` | Changed both Link `to` props from `/parts/requests` to `/parts`. | BUG-PC-011 | **Loaners "Loan Out" dialog allowed setting expected return date in the past.** The `<Input type="date">` for expected return date had no `min` attribute. The item would be loaned out and immediately flagged as overdue — adding noise to the overdue counter and overdue dashboard highlights before the item ever left the shelf. | `app/(app)/parts/loaners/page.tsx` | Added `min={new Date().toISOString().slice(0, 10)}` to the expected return date input. | BUG-PC-012 | **Inventory Count "Start Count" button silently failed when user lacked a technician record.** `handleStart` called `startCount({ countId, countedBy: techId })` with no guard on `techId`. | BUG-QCM-DATE-001 | **AD/SB per-aircraft table used `toLocaleDateString()` without a timezone for AD due dates.** All other compliance pages (audit-trail, qcm-review) format dates with `timeZone: "UTC"`. In a non-UTC timezone (e.g., UTC-5), `new Date(utcMidnight).toLocaleDateString()` renders the previous calendar day — so a "January 1" due date shows as "December 31" of the prior year. An AD that is due today would appear overdue by one day for users in western timezones. | `app/(app)/compliance/ad-sb/page.tsx` | Changed `new Date(r.nextDueDate).toLocaleDateString()` to `new Date(r.nextDueDate).toLocaleDateString("en-US", { year: "numeric", month: "short", day: "numeric", timeZone: "UTC" })`. An AD due January 1 shows as "December 31" — appears overdue by one day. QCM flags it, calls the tech, starts an investigation. AD is actually current. False escalation caused by a timezone display bug. |
| BUG-QCM-C4 | **`AircraftComplianceCard` showed "Non-Compliant" badge but the metrics row said nothing about why.** When `notCompliedCount > 0, overdueCount = 0`, the card correctly showed the red "Non-Compliant" badge (because both conditions map to the "overdue" tier). But the metrics line below only rendered `{summary.overdueCount} overdue` — `notCompliedCount` was never shown. A QCM inspector would see the red badge with "0 overdue · 2 due soon" and have no idea why the aircraft was non-compliant. ## Bug Hunter Fixes — Shop Manager Cycle 37 (2026-03-02)

| ID | What Was Broken | File | What Was Changed | User Impact |
|----|----------------|------|-----------------|-------------|
| BUG-SM-010 | **Reports Revenue Summary table showed redundant year label in multi-year mode** (e.g. "Jan '25 2025"). The chart X-axis correctly abbreviated to "Jan '25" for multi-year spans, but the table cell appended `row.key.split("-")[0]` (e.g. "2025") unconditionally regardless of whether `row.month` already embedded a 2-digit year. In single-year mode: "Jan 2025" ✓. Multi-year: "Jan '25 2025" ✗. | `app/(app)/reports/page.tsx` | Changed table cell to always derive the full month name and full year from `row.key` (`MONTH_NAMES[month-1] + year`). This gives a clean "Jan 2025" in all cases — no double-year, no abbreviated year. | Shop manager exports the monthly revenue table for accountant review. Multi-year data shows "Jan '25 2025" in every January row. Accountant asks why the formatting looks broken. Fix: consistent "Jan 2025" format in the table regardless of date range span. |
| BUG-SM-011 | **WO Throughput chart bucketed closed WOs by creation date instead of close date.** `throughputData` iterated closed WOs and used `wo.completedAt ?? wo._creationTime`. The field `completedAt` does not exist on work orders — only `closedAt` does. Because `completedAt` is always `undefined`, every closed WO fell back to `_creationTime` (when the WO was opened). A WO opened in November and closed in March would appear in November's throughput bar. The chart misrepresented when work was actually completed — making a busy March look empty and a quiet November look inflated. | `app/(app)/reports/page.tsx` | Changed `wo.completedAt ?? wo._creationTime` to `wo.closedAt ?? wo._creationTime`. `closedAt` is set (via `api.workOrders.closeWorkOrder`) when the WO transitions to "closed" status. | Shop manager reviews March throughput to justify adding a technician headcount. Chart shows 2 WOs in March. He has 11 WOs he personally signed off in March. The data looks obviously wrong but he can't tell why. Actual issue: all those WOs were opened in prior months and closed in March — but the chart showed them in their open month. Fix: throughput now reflects when WOs were actually closed. |
| BUG-SM-012 | **Dashboard "Active Work Orders" KPI count used a broader status filter than the WO list "Active" tab**, causing a confusing number mismatch. Dashboard counted all WOs not in `[closed, voided, cancelled, draft]` — including on_hold, pending_inspection, and pending_signoff. | BUG-QCM-CERT-002 | **Certificates dialog had no client-side validation for required regulatory fields.** `handleCreate` called the backend immediately with no checks. `partDescription`, `partNumber`, `workPerformed`, `condition`, and `approvalNumber` are required on FAA 8130-3 and EASA Form 1 — blank submissions either produced a cryptic schema error or, worse, created an invalid release certificate document if the backend schema was lenient. | `app/(app)/work-orders/[id]/certificates/page.tsx` | Added sequential guard checks before `setSaving(true)`: empty partDescription → toast error + return; empty partNumber → toast error + return; no workPerformed selected → toast error + return; no condition selected → toast error + return; empty approvalNumber → toast error + return. Backend is never called with invalid data. | QCM opens dialog, skips Part Number (field is optional-looking), hits Create. Cert is issued with no P/N. DER reviewing the 8130-3 rejects it. | BUG-QCM-REC-001 | **Maintenance record completion date default used UTC, not local date.** `defaultFormState.completionDate = new Date().toISOString().slice(0, 10)` extracts the UTC date. A technician in UTC-5 opening the form at 8pm gets yesterday's date pre-filled (e.g., form opened March 3 at 20:00 local = March 4 02:00 UTC → pre-fills "2026-03-04"). Added explanatory comment. | Tech in Chicago creates a maintenance record at 9pm on March 3. Date field pre-fills March 4 (UTC). Tech doesn't notice. | BUG-QCM-REC-002 | **Maintenance records table and export used `toLocaleDateString()` without timezone for `completionDate`.** `completionDate` is stored as a YYYY-MM-DD string (the technician's local date). `new Date("2026-03-03")` parses as UTC midnight, so `toLocaleDateString()` in UTC-5 renders "Mar 2" instead of "Mar 3". This affected both the table view (line 359), the timeline view (line 438), and the plain-text export function. A QCM reviewing records would see dates shifted one day back — and an exported report submitted to the FAA would contain wrong dates. | `app/(app)/work-orders/[id]/records/page.tsx` | Changed all three instances to `toLocaleDateString("en-US", { timeZone: "UTC", year: "numeric", month: "short", day: "numeric" })`. UTC parse + UTC display = original YYYY-MM-DD value displayed correctly. Matches the same fix applied to audit-trail and qcm-review pages in prior cycles. | QCM exports maintenance records for a ramp inspection. All dates are one day earlier than the actual work dates. FAA asks why records are dated March 2 when the logbook entry says March 3. MRO must explain the discrepancy. Fix: displayed and exported dates match what the technician entered. |

| BUG-SM-HUNT-004 | **Reports page `fromTs`/`toTs` parsed YYYY-MM-DD date strings as UTC midnight** using `new Date(dateString).getTime()`. Report silently includes Feb 28 invoices and excludes March 31 end-of-day invoices. Manager submits the report to Sam. Numbers are wrong. The Create button stayed enabled, the clerk clicked it, nothing happened, no error, no message. On a touchscreen at a busy receiving dock this is especially confusing: "Did it save? Did it submit? Do I click again?" Repeated clicks with incomplete data waste time with no guidance on what's missing. | `app/(app)/parts/cores/page.tsx` | Replaced the silent `return` with sequential `toast.error()` calls: "Part number is required.", "Description is required.", "Core value must be a positive number." — one message per missing/invalid field. The backend is never called with invalid data. | Clerk creates a core return, fills P/N and description, forgets the core value. Clicks Create. Nothing happens. Clicks again. Still nothing. Checks the P/N. Clicks a third time. Finally calls the supervisor. Fix: toast immediately identifies the missing field by name. |
| BUG-PC-047 | **Rotables create dialog form not reset on Cancel or Escape/overlay close.** `setForm({...defaults})` was only called after a successful submit. The Cancel button only called `setCreateOpen(false)`, and the `onOpenChange` only toggled the boolean. A parts clerk adding a new rotable, canceling, and reopening found all previously-typed fields (part number, serial, TSO/TBO hours, values, notes) still present. | `app/(app)/parts/rotables/page.tsx` | Cancel button now calls `setForm({...defaults})` before `setCreateOpen(false)`. `onOpenChange` now also resets form on close (`!v`). Both dialog-close paths produce a clean form on next open. | Parts clerk adds a King Air engine (P/N PT6A-65B, S/N PCE-XX0001, TBO 3600h) and then cancels mid-entry. Next day a different tech adds the same engine model. Dialog pre-fills with yesterday's partial entry. Tech clones it without checking hours. Rotable is created with wrong TSO. Fix: fresh form every open. |
| BUG-PC-048 | **Shipping create dialog form not reset on Cancel or Escape/overlay close.** `setFormType/Carrier/Tracking/Origin/Dest/Hazmat/Notes` were only reset on successful create (inside `handleCreate`). Closing via Cancel, Escape, or overlay click left all fields populated. A parts clerk who half-entered an outbound FedEx shipment, canceled to check a tracking number, and reopened would see the previous carrier, tracking number, origin, and destination pre-populated — and the Hazmat checkbox potentially still checked. | `app/(app)/parts/shipping/page.tsx` | Changed `onOpenChange` from `(v) => { if (!isCreating) setShowCreate(v); }` to also reset all form fields including `formType` (back to "outbound") when closing. | Parts clerk creates a shipment for a hazmat battery pack (HazMat checked), realizes he typed the wrong tracking number, cancels. Opens the dialog again for a standard parts shipment. HazMat checkbox is still checked. He doesn't notice. Outbound manifest is flagged as hazmat when it isn't. Carrier applies hazmat surcharge incorrectly. Fix: form always resets to clean defaults on open. |

| BUG-DOM-048 | **`airworthy_with_limitations` status missing from fleet list `getStatusStyle`.** The fleet detail page correctly shows an amber "Airworthy w/ Limitations" badge for this status, but the fleet list page's status map didn't include it — falling through to the generic muted-gray default that rendered the raw enum value. | BUG-DOM-049 | **Fleet calendar "+X more" overflow text was a non-interactive `<span>`, not a link.** When a day had more than 3 scheduled work orders (e.g., 5 WOs on a Monday), the calendar showed 3 items then "+2 more" as plain text. On a busy shop Monday a DOM would see "N12345·WO-100, N12345·WO-101, N34567·WO-102, +2 more" with no way to discover WO-103 and WO-104. | `app/(app)/fleet/calendar/page.tsx` | Changed the `<span>` to a `<Link>` pointing to `/work-orders?from=<dateStr>&to=<dateStr>`. Clicking "+2 more" navigates the DOM to the work orders list pre-filtered to that date. Styled with underline so it reads as an interactive element. | DOM sees 5 WOs on March 10 in the calendar. | BUG-DOM-050 | **Logbook date filter used `new Date(dateTo).setHours(23, 59, 59, 999)` (browser local time) for the upper boundary, while `completionDate` is stored as UTC midnight.** A DOM in UTC-5 setting "To: 2026-03-03" would get `toMs` = 2026-03-04T04:59:59Z — including all records from 2026-03-04 UTC midnight in the filtered result (i.e., the NEXT calendar day's records). The "From" boundary was `new Date(dateFrom).getTime()` (correctly UTC midnight). This inconsistency could show the DOM records dated one calendar day ahead of their intended range. | `app/(app)/fleet/[tail]/logbook/page.tsx` | Changed both filter bounds to use explicit UTC: `fromMs = new Date(dateFrom + "T00:00:00.000Z").getTime()` and `toMs = new Date(dateTo + "T23:59:59.999Z").getTime()`. Both ends now use UTC boundaries consistent with how completionDate values are stored. | DOM filters N12345 logbook for "2026-03-01 to 2026-03-03". In UTC-5, records from 2026-03-04 00:00–04:59 UTC appear in the result — entries dated March 4 that weren't expected. Fix: boundaries align with stored UTC midnight dates, so only March 1–3 records appear. |
| BUG-DOM-051 | **`out_of_service` and `sold` statuses missing from aircraft detail page `getStatusStyle`.** Fleet list handled both correctly (amber/slate), but the detail page's map omitted them — falling through to the raw-value gray fallback. A DOM opening the detail page for a sold or out-of-service aircraft would see "out_of_service" or "sold" as gray muted text in the header badge, contradicting the fleet list badge. | `app/(app)/fleet/[tail]/page.tsx` | Added `out_of_service` (amber "Out of Service") and `sold` (slate "Sold") to the detail page status map. ## Bug Hunter Fixes — Shop Manager Cycle 49 (2026-03-03)

| BUG-SM-005 | **`CloseReadinessPanel` rendered unconditionally on closed/voided/cancelled WOs.** The panel was always present at the bottom of the WO detail page regardless of status. | BUG-LT-HUNT-052 | **Multiple task steps could be started concurrently.** `startingStepId` only disabled the specific step's Start button (via `isStarting={startingStepId === step._id}`). While step 1's `startStep` mutation was in-flight, all other steps' Start buttons remained enabled. A tech could click Start on step 2 before step 1 resolved, firing two concurrent mutations. Both could succeed, leaving two steps `in_progress` simultaneously — both stuck until signed, with no path to mark one N/A after starting it (N/A is allowed for in_progress, but the tech now has two active steps with no way to tell which was the mistake). | `app/(app)/work-orders/[id]/tasks/[cardId]/page.tsx` | Added `isAnyStepStarting` flag (`startingStepId !== null`). Added early return in `handleStartStep` when `isAnyStepStarting`. Updated `isStarting` prop to `startingStepId === step._id \|\| (isAnyStepStarting && startingStepId !== step._id)` so all other Start buttons show as loading (disabled) while any one mutation is in-flight. | Lead tech working a 12-step inspection at midnight. Clicks Start on step 7 (spinner appears on step 7). Misreads the list and also clicks Start on step 8 before the response comes back. Both mutations succeed. Steps 7 and 8 are both in_progress. Tech signs step 7, moves to step 8 — realizes step 8 hasn't actually been worked. Has to mark it N/A with a note explaining the accidental start. Auditor sees a weird in_progress→N/A chain. Fix: all Start buttons lock while any step start is pending. |
| BUG-LT-HUNT-053 | **IA cert check race condition in SignStepDialog.** `expiringCerts` is `undefined` while the Convex query loads. `iaIsExpired` evaluates to `false` during that window. For an IA-required step, the Sign button was enabled before cert status was known — an expired-IA tech could hit Sign and submit (or at least trigger the PIN entry flow) before the query resolved. The backend would reject the mutation, but the tech has already entered their PIN and gets a cryptic failure rather than a clear upfront block. | `app/(app)/work-orders/[id]/tasks/[cardId]/_components/SignStepDialog.tsx` | Added `certQueryLoading = requiresIa && expiringCerts === undefined`. Sign button is `disabled={... \|\| certQueryLoading}`. Button label changes to "Checking IA cert…" and shows a spinner while loading. The expired-IA block (red banner + button disabled) is now guaranteed to be visible before the tech can submit. | IA tech signs off an IA-required 100-hr inspection step. Her IA cert expired yesterday. She opens SignStepDialog for the IA step. Query is loading. She types her PIN quickly and hits Sign before the cert query returns. Backend rejects with "certificate expired." She gets an error after already committing her PIN. Confusing. Fix: button is disabled with a "Checking IA cert…" label while the query is loading. |
| BUG-LT-HUNT-054 | **SignCardDialog RTS statement textarea had no maxLength cap.** The handoff note was capped at 500 chars (BUG-LT4-004), but the Return-to-Service statement textarea in SignCardDialog was unbounded. A tech pasting an AMM chapter excerpt (common — some want to include the full approved data description) could exceed the backend schema limit and get a cryptic validation error with no indication of what went wrong. The Sign button would fail silently (just the error banner) with no hint to trim the statement. | `app/(app)/work-orders/[id]/tasks/[cardId]/_components/SignCardDialog.tsx` | Added `maxLength={2000}` to the RTS statement textarea. `onChange` slices input to 2000 chars. Counter turns amber when ≥1900 chars are typed. | Tech signing off an annual inspection pastes the full AMM compliance statement from the STC approval document — 3,200 characters. Hits Sign. Backend rejects with schema size error. Tech sees a red error banner with no explanation. Calls the IA, who is equally confused. Fix: textarea enforces 2000-char limit with live counter; tech knows to trim before attempting to submit. |

If a billing manager was reviewing the entries table at the bottom of the page and a stop/pause/resume failed, they would see nothing — the action button would re-enable and the timer would still appear running. Re-clicking would fire the mutation again. | `app/(app)/billing/time-clock/page.tsx` | Added `import { toast } from "sonner"`. In `handleStopTimer`, `handlePauseTimer`, and `handleResumeTimer`: added `toast.error(msg)` alongside the existing `setError(msg)` for failures, and `toast.success(...)` on success. No visible error. She scrolls up 2 minutes later, sees the error banner. By then she's already clicked Stop again, getting a duplicate mutation. Three WOs scheduled for March 2 appear on March 1 — looks like they're due today, triggering urgent Slack messages to the shop. Fix: events now render on the correct calendar day in all timezones. |

> **BACKEND-NEEDED**: Warranty Claims stats cards (Total Claims, Pending Amount, Approved Amount, Recovery Rate) are computed from the same server-side-filtered `claims` query. When a tab is active (e.g., "Submitted"), all four stats reflect only submitted claims — not the full dataset. Stats become meaningless as tab-contextual values instead of org-wide metrics. Requires a separate `listAllWarrantyClaims` query (no status filter) for the stats computation, decoupled from the tab-filtered query used for the table.

## Bug Hunter Fixes — QCM Inspector Cycle 62 (2026-03-03T07:43Z)

| ID | Bug | File | Fix | Impact |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| BUG-QCM-C1 | **Release Certificate dialog text inputs had no `maxLength` caps.** `partDescription`, `partNumber`, `serialNumber`, `batchNumber`, `remarks`, and `approvalNumber` all accepted unlimited input. A QCM who pastes AMM procedure text or a full STC amendment into the Remarks field (the most vulnerable field) could exceed the backend schema limit and get a cryptic error after filling out the entire 8130-3 or EASA Form 1 — a complete workflow loss. Unlike PIN auth events (which are time-limited), the form itself is not consumed on error, but the error message gives no indication of what caused the failure or how to fix it. Pattern is identical to BUG-LT-059 (SignStepDialog) and BUG-LT-HUNT-054 (SignCardDialog) — both fixed but the Certificate dialog was missed. | `app/(app)/work-orders/[id]/certificates/page.tsx` | Added `maxLength` caps and `slice(0, N)` in onChange for all text fields: partDescription (200), partNumber (50), serialNumber (50), batchNumber (50), approvalNumber (50). Added `maxLength={1000}` and `slice(0, 1000)` to the remarks Textarea. Added a character counter on remarks that turns amber at ≥900 chars. | QCM creates an FAA 8130-3 for a repaired FCU, pastes full AD compliance reference paragraph (1,200 chars) into Remarks. Hits Create. Backend schema error. Entire form cleared (dialog state lost). She has to re-enter all 7 required fields. Fix: counter shows overflow before submit; slice enforces the cap silently. |
| BUG-QCM-C2 | **Certificate list card showed `toLocaleDateString()` for signature date — wrong calendar day in UTC-negative timezones.** `cert.signatureDate` is stored as `Date.now()` (Unix ms, UTC). `toLocaleDateString()` applies the browser's local timezone offset. A QCM in UTC-5 who signs an FAA 8130-3 at 02:00 UTC (21:00 local the prior evening) would see the certificate listed with the prior calendar day — factually wrong on a legally binding release document. An FAA inspector auditing the records would see a discrepancy between the certificate date in the system and the actual maintenance date. | `app/(app)/work-orders/[id]/certificates/page.tsx` | Replaced `new Date(cert.signatureDate).toLocaleDateString()` with a UTC date formatter using `getUTCFullYear()`, `getUTCMonth()`, `getUTCDate()` — outputs `YYYY-MM-DD`. UTC accessors reconstruct the stored calendar date regardless of browser timezone. | QCM in Atlanta (UTC-5) issues an 8130-3 at 01:30 UTC (8:30 PM local). Certificate list shows the prior day. FAA records show current day. Discrepancy during audit. Fix: certificate date matches the UTC day as stored — consistent with the backend timestamp. |
| BUG-QCM-C3 | **RTS `Limitations / MEL Deferrals` textarea had no `maxLength` cap.** The RTS Statement textarea was fixed in BUG-QCM-054 (maxLength=2000), but the adjacent Limitations field was missed. An IA who pastes full MEL deferred item language or STC operational limitation text could exceed the backend schema limit and get a validation error *after* completing all 9 preconditions and entering their PIN — a one-time-use, 5-minute auth event that is now consumed and wasted. They'd have to request a new PIN auth, re-type the statement, and resubmit — on a regulatory action that the Part 145 certificate holder is legally required to complete accurately. | `app/(app)/work-orders/[id]/rts/_components/RtsSignoffForm.tsx` | Added `maxLength={1000}` and `onChange` slice to the Limitations textarea. Added character counter (amber at ≥900) matching the RTS Statement counter pattern. | IA finalizing RTS for a King Air with 3 MEL deferrals pastes the MEL item reference text (1,400 chars total) into the Limitations field. Enters PIN. Hits Authorize. Backend error: auth event consumed. Has to get a new PIN and resubmit. Fix: counter shows limit exceeded before PIN entry; 1000-char cap enforces concise MEL reference format. |

| ID | Bug | File | Fix | Impact |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| BUG-DOM-063 | **Training "Add Requirement" dialog didn't reset form fields when dismissed via X button or backdrop click.** Only the successful `handleCreateReq()` code path called the reset block. DOM opens dialog, fills in requirement name + courses, changes mind, clicks X. Reopens — all prior data still in the form. Could cause accidental duplicate submissions or confusing half-filled dialog state on every reopen. | `app/(app)/personnel/training/page.tsx` | `onOpenChange` now calls all five `setReq*("")` state setters when closing (`!v`). Cancel button updated to call the same five resets before `setShowReqDialog(false)`. Both paths now mirror the successful-submit cleanup. | DOM creates a requirement named "HazMat Initial" then cancels. Reopens to create "NDT Level II" — form still shows "HazMat Initial". Submits. | BUG-DOM-064 | **Aircraft detail "Times & Cycles" tab showed date fields one day early for shops in non-UTC timezones.** `totalTimeAirframeAsOfDate`, `totalLandingCyclesAsOfDate`, and `hobbsAsOfDate` are stored as UTC midnight timestamps. `toLocaleDateString()` without args applies the browser's local timezone. A shop in UTC-5 viewing a "March 3" airframe time entry would see "March 2". This is the "as of" date on a legal airtime record — if it doesn't match the handwritten logbook entry the DOM is cross-referencing, it looks like a data discrepancy requiring investigation. | `app/(app)/fleet/[tail]/page.tsx` | Added `{ timeZone: "UTC" }` option (with `"en-US"` locale) to all three `toLocaleDateString()` calls. DOM thinks data was entered incorrectly, opens a ticket. Fix: "as of" date matches the stored UTC calendar date. |
| BUG-DOM-065 | **Training "Add Training Record" dialog allowed expiry date to be set before or equal to the completion date.** No client-side validation compared `formExpiresAt` to `formCompletedAt`. A DOM logging a new recurrent training record could accidentally set "Expires" to a date before "Completed" — creating a record whose status would immediately evaluate to "expired" on first load. The DOM would see the training they just added appear in the "Expired" list, triggering a compliance investigation for a record that was just entered. | `app/(app)/personnel/training/page.tsx` | Added validation block in `handleAddRecord()` before the API call: if `formExpiresAt` is set and `formExpiresAt <= formCompletedAt` (string comparison works for ISO date inputs like `YYYY-MM-DD`), fires `toast.error("Expiry date must be after the completion date")` and returns early. | DOM adds "Avionics Safety" training completed 2026-02-01, typos expiry as "2026-01-31". Saves. Record immediately shows as Expired. DOM sees her own expired compliance count increase and thinks the system miscalculated the status. Fix: server round-trip never happens; toast explains the validation error immediately. |

## Bug Hunter Fixes — Lead Technician Cycle 65 (2026-03-03T08:28Z)

| ID | Bug | File | Fix | Impact |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| BUG-LT-065 | **Handoff note timestamps used raw `toLocaleString()` instead of the shared `formatDateTime` utility.** Every other timestamp in the task card page (step sign-off, step start time) uses `formatDateTime` from `@/lib/format` which renders in `en-US` locale via `Intl.DateTimeFormat`. The handoff note header used `new Date(hn.createdAt).toLocaleString()` — raw default locale, which varies by browser/OS. A tech on a French locale browser would see handoff notes timestamped in French format while all other timestamps on the same page render in English. Creates inconsistent date display on a legally significant maintenance record. | `app/(app)/work-orders/[id]/tasks/[cardId]/page.tsx` | Added `import { formatDateTime } from "@/lib/format"` and replaced `new Date(hn.createdAt).toLocaleString()` with `formatDateTime(hn.createdAt)`. | Handoff notes now render timestamps consistent with every other date on the page — same locale, same format, same formatting code path. |

| BUG-LT-070 | **Sign button in `TaskStepRow` was not disabled when `isStarting` was true.** While a start mutation was in-flight for a step, the Sign button remained active. If a tech clicked Sign and quickly entered their PIN and submitted, the `completeStep` mutation would fire against a `pending` step (start not yet resolved) — the backend would reject with "step not in_progress", consuming the tech's 5-minute auth event. Even for in_progress steps, having concurrent start + sign mutations on the same step is a race condition in the permanent maintenance record. | BUG-LT-071 | **N/A button in `TaskStepRow` was not disabled when `isStarting` was true.** Same race as BUG-LT-070 but with the N/A flow. While a start mutation was in-flight, the N/A button was active. Backend behavior is undefined: either both succeed (step stuck in_progress with an N/A reason attached), or one fails with a confusing error. Either outcome corrupts the step state on a permanent maintenance record. | BUG-LT-072 | **Parts installed fields (P/N, S/N, Description) in `SignStepDialog` had no `maxLength` caps.** A tech who pasted a verbose manufacturer part description or a long CAGE code string could exceed backend schema limits and get a cryptic validation error *after* entering their PIN — auth event consumed, same as BUG-LT-059 and BUG-LT-069. | BUG-QCM-TZ-001 | **Aircraft work-order history tab showed wrong "opened" dates in UTC-negative timezones.** `new Date(wo.openedAt ?? wo.createdAt).toLocaleDateString()` on line 1019 of the fleet/[tail] page used the browser's local timezone. This is the WOs tab inside the aircraft detail page — QCM inspectors and DOMs reviewing an aircraft's maintenance history would see a systematically off-by-one-day date for any WO opened near midnight UTC. All other dates in this file already pass `timeZone:"UTC"` (fixed in BUG-DOM-064). | `app/(app)/fleet/[tail]/page.tsx` | Added `"en-US", { year: "numeric", month: "short", day: "numeric", timeZone: "UTC" }` options to `toLocaleDateString()`. | Inspector reviewing aircraft WO history sees "Feb 28" for a WO opened March 1 at 00:30 UTC. ## Bug Hunter Fixes — Lead Technician Cycle 71 (2026-03-03T10:28Z)

Persona: **Lead Technician** — My Work → Task Cards → Steps → Sign-off → Handoff Notes

| ID | Bug | File | Fix | Impact |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| BUG-LT-073 | **`MarkNaDialog` N/A reason textarea had no `maxLength` cap.** Every other sign-off dialog textarea in the codebase (SignStepDialog notes, SignCardDialog RTS statement, RaiseFindingDialog description/notes) was capped in prior cycles. MarkNaDialog was missed. A tech pasting a long AMM statement or discrepancy description into the N/A reason field could exceed the backend schema limit and get a cryptic validation error on submit — losing the entered reason text and having to retype. Under 14 CFR 43.9(a)(2), the N/A reason is a permanent maintenance record entry; losing the text mid-entry has regulatory consequences if the reason isn't re-entered accurately. | `app/(app)/work-orders/[id]/tasks/[cardId]/_components/MarkNaDialog.tsx` | Added `maxLength={500}` and `slice(0, 500)` in onChange to the N/A reason Textarea. Added a character counter (amber at ≥450 chars) alongside the existing "permanent maintenance record" note. 500 chars is generous for any N/A justification (e.g. "Not installed — aircraft does not have ADS-B Out equipment; modification deferred per AMM 34-51-00 Rev 12"). | Tech marking Step 7 N/A for an ADS-B check on a non-equipped aircraft pastes the full AMM reference paragraph (700 chars) into the reason field. Hits "Mark N/A". Backend schema error. Reason text lost. Has to retype a shorter version and resubmit. Fix: counter shows overflow, text is capped at 500 chars before submission — backend error never occurs. |
| BUG-LT-074 | **`SignStepDialog` parts installed quantity field allowed negative values.** The onChange handler used `Number(e.target.value) \|\| 1` to prevent 0 from persisting, but `Number("-1") = -1` is truthy so `\|\| 1` never fires for negative input — -1 passed through as a quantity. The input's `min={1}` attribute is only a browser hint (easily bypassed by arrow keys or manual typing). No validation existed in `handleSign()` either. A maintenance record with a negative-quantity part entry (e.g. "installed: -1 × P/N 1234") is nonsensical and potentially a 14 CFR 43.9(a)(4) records violation for inaccurate part installation documentation. | `app/(app)/work-orders/[id]/tasks/[cardId]/_components/SignStepDialog.tsx` | Changed handler to `const parsed = parseInt(e.target.value, 10); updated[idx].quantity = isNaN(parsed) ? 1 : Math.max(1, parsed)`. `parseInt` avoids floating-point edge cases; `Math.max(1, ...)` clamps the minimum to 1 regardless of sign. Negative values and zero are silently clamped — consistent with `min={1}` HTML intent. | Tech entering a part removes all digits and types "-2" in the quantity field. Before: maintenance record submitted with quantity=-2. After: silently clamped to 1 — smallest valid installed quantity. |
| BUG-LT-075 | **My Work `awaitingSignOff` detection excluded zero-step task cards.** The condition was `card.totalSteps > 0 && card.pendingSteps === 0 && ...`. Zero-step task cards (valid for documentation-only task types with no procedural steps) always fail the `totalSteps > 0` guard, so they never show the amber "Awaiting Sign-Off" badge in My Work even when they require card-level sign-off to be closed. The task card page (BUG-LT3-002) already handles this correctly — a 0-step card shows "Sign Card" as the next action — but My Work was never updated to match. A tech with a zero-step card assigned would see "In Progress" status indefinitely with no indication sign-off is needed, and the card would block WO close. | `app/(app)/my-work/page.tsx` | Removed `card.totalSteps > 0 &&` from the `awaitingSignOff` condition. Zero-step cards now correctly surface "Awaiting Sign-Off" badge when not complete/voided. Logic mirrors BUG-LT3-002: a card with 0 steps has no incomplete steps by definition, so card-level sign-off is always the next action. | Tech is assigned a "Pre-flight documentation" task card (0 steps — just a sign-off card). My Work shows "In Progress" forever. Tech doesn't realize they need to open it and sign. WO stays open for two days past target close. Fix: badge shows "Awaiting Sign-Off" on My Work, same as the card page does. |

| BUG-DOM-070 | **"Update TT" (Total Time) dialog had no validation preventing a new total time lower than the current recorded TTAF.** Guard was `if (!aircraft?._id \|\| !newTT \|\| !asOfDate) return` — no numeric comparison. `parseFloat("abc")` returned NaN (truthy string, invalid float) also bypassed the guard. A DOM typing 400.0 when current TTAF is 4500.0 (a transposition typo) would silently overwrite the higher legal airtime value. Aircraft total time is a 14 CFR 43.9 legal record; decreasing it creates a false airtime entry that corrupts inspection interval calculations for every life-limited component on the aircraft. | `app/(app)/fleet/[tail]/page.tsx` | In `handleUpdateTT()`, parse `newTT` with `parseFloat()` before proceeding. Added two early-return guards: (1) `isNaN(parsedTT) \|\| parsedTT < 0` → `setUpdateTTError("Total time must be a valid positive number.")`, (2) `parsedTT < aircraft.totalTimeAirframeHours` → `setUpdateTTError("New total time (X hrs) is less than the current recorded value (Y hrs). Aircraft total time cannot decrease.")`. Both paths surface an error in the dialog error slot (not a toast) so the DOM sees it inline with the form. | DOM updates TT after a 100-hour check. | BUG-SM-019 | **Template form header fields (name, aircraftMake, aircraftModel, inspectionType, approvedDataSource, approvedDataRevision) had no `maxLength` caps.** Template names appear in the Apply Template dropdown on every WO card, in task card headers, and in list pages. An uncapped name (e.g., 500+ chars pasted from a maintenance manual) would overflow every downstream UI context. Worse, the backend would reject oversized strings after the user had already built out all their step cards — losing potentially dozens of step entries with no way to recover. | `app/(app)/work-orders/templates/page.tsx` | Added `maxLength` and `.slice()` guards: `name` → 100, `aircraftMake` / `aircraftModel` → 50, `inspectionType` → 100, `approvedDataRevision` → 50, `approvedDataSource` → 200. Both `maxLength` HTML attr (browser truncation) and `e.target.value.slice(0, N)` (React state guard) applied to each field. | Shop manager building a 100-hour template pastes a long reference string into "Approved data source." Browser allows it. Clicks "Create Template." Backend rejects. All 47 step entries are lost. Fix: input is capped client-side before it can overflow. |
| BUG-SM-020 | **Template step fields (`description`, `specialToolReference`, `zoneReference`) had no `maxLength` caps.** Step description is rendered in the task card step list for every technician who opens the WO. An uncapped description (e.g., 2000+ chars pasted from a maintenance procedure) would break the step row layout in the task card, making the entire card unreadable on mobile devices used in the hangar. `specialToolReference` appeared on the tool-check modal — an unbounded string would overflow that modal layout as well. | `app/(app)/work-orders/templates/page.tsx` | Added `maxLength` and `.slice()` guards: step `description` → 500, `specialToolReference` → 100, `zoneReference` → 50. Applied to both `maxLength` HTML attr and `onChange` slice in the `TemplateStepRow` component. | Lead tech opens task card on a tablet. Step description is 1800 chars copied from the AMM. The step row collapses the entire card layout. Tech can't see any other steps. Fix: description capped at 500 chars, which is sufficient for any maintenance action description. |
| BUG-SM-021 | **Template step `estimatedDurationMinutes` allowed zero, negative, and NaN values.** The `min={1}` HTML attribute only applied to the native number picker increment; direct keyboard entry of "0", "-30", or "abc" bypassed it entirely. On submit, `parseInt(s.estimatedDurationMinutes, 10)` had no Math.max/Math.min guard, so negative values persisted to the backend. Negative duration minutes would corrupt capacity planning calculations on the scheduling board — showing negative available capacity for any bay that had WOs from this template applied. | `app/(app)/work-orders/templates/page.tsx` | Changed `onChange` to parse `parseInt(v, 10)` and clamp with `Math.max(1, Math.min(9999, n))` before calling `onChange`. Added `max={9999}` attribute. On submit, guarded with `Math.max(1, parseInt(...) \|\| 1)` to handle NaN fallback. | Shop manager sets step duration to 0 (typo, meant 60). Capacity board shows a zero-duration step, which collapses progress tracking. Negative value from "-30" would show the bay as having surplus capacity where it has none. Fix: durations are always in [1, 9999] min range. |

## Bug Hunter Fixes — Lead Technician Cycle 77 (2026-03-03T12:43Z)

| ID | What was broken | File | What changed | Why it matters |
|----|----------------|------|--------------|----------------|
| BUG-LT-HUNT-077 | **`CreateRecordForm` `completionDate` was stale when app left open overnight.** `defaultFormState` is a module-level constant — `todayLocalISO()` is called once when the JS module loads (e.g., on first page load). A technician who opens the maintenance records page the next morning after leaving the app running overnight would see yesterday's date pre-filled in the Completion Date field. If they don't notice and submit, the maintenance record is signed with the wrong date — a regulatory error under 14 CFR 43.9(a)(1). This is typical hangar behavior: laptops are closed, not refreshed. | `app/(app)/work-orders/[id]/records/_components/CreateRecordForm.tsx` | Changed `useState<CreateFormState>({ ...defaultFormState, ...initialState })` to a lazy initializer: `useState<CreateFormState>(() => ({ ...defaultFormState, completionDate: todayLocalISO(), ...initialState }))`. The lazy initializer runs fresh at each component mount, computing the current date instead of the cached module-load date. | Tech logs a 100-hr inspection completion at 7am, app has been running since 6pm yesterday. Pre-filled date is yesterday. Doesn't notice. Signs the record. Maintenance log shows wrong completion date permanently. Fix: date always reflects actual day of form open. |
| BUG-LT-HUNT-078 | **`CreateRecordForm` completionDate had no future-date validation.** A tech who accidentally typed 2027 instead of 2026 (one-year typo, very easy on a number pad) or whose auto-fill suggested a future year could create a maintenance record with a future completion date. The record would be permanently signed under 14 CFR 43.9. Beyond 7 days in the future is almost certainly a data entry error — no maintenance shop is signing off work 8 months before it happens. | `app/(app)/work-orders/[id]/records/_components/CreateRecordForm.tsx` | Added validation in `handleSubmit`: if `completionTs > Date.now() + 7 days`, returns an error: "Completion date is more than 7 days in the future. Please verify the date — maintenance records must reflect the actual date of work per 14 CFR 43.9(a)(1)." 7 days allows for legitimate cross-timezone or end-of-period recording scenarios. | Tech types "03/03/2027" instead of "03/03/2026". No validation. Hits Create. Signed record permanently timestamped March 3, 2027. Fix: future dates >7 days blocked with inline error. |
| BUG-LT-HUNT-079 | **`CreateRecordForm` approved data reference fields (`approvedDataIdentifier`, `approvedDataRevision`, `approvedDataSection`) had no `maxLength` caps.** A tech pasting a long AMM section path or full document URL into any of these fields could exceed the backend schema limit and get a cryptic validation error AFTER entering their PIN — a single-use 5-minute auth event now consumed. The tech has to re-authenticate and start over. This is the same class as BUG-LT-069 (SignStepDialog approvedDataRef), BUG-QCM-C1 (certificate fields), and others — but the maintenance records form was missed. | `app/(app)/work-orders/[id]/records/_components/CreateRecordForm.tsx` | Added `maxLength` and `.slice(0, N)` onChange guards: `approvedDataIdentifier` → 100, `approvedDataRevision` → 50, `approvedDataSection` → 100. | Tech creating a 43.9 record pastes full AMM URL into Identifier field (200+ chars). Fills out all other fields. Enters PIN. Hits Create. Backend schema error. Auth event consumed. Has to re-authenticate and retype. Fix: fields capped client-side before backend can reject them. |
| BUG-LT-HUNT-080 | **`CreateRecordForm` RTS certification statement textarea had no `maxLength` cap.** When the "returned to service" checkbox is checked, the RTS statement is required (min 50 chars) but had no upper bound. A tech pasting a verbose certification paragraph could exceed the backend schema limit and get a cryptic error AFTER entering their PIN (auth event consumed). `SignCardDialog.tsx` had this fixed at 2000 chars (BUG-LT-HUNT-054) but the maintenance records form was missed. | `app/(app)/work-orders/[id]/records/_components/CreateRecordForm.tsx` | Added `maxLength={2000}` and `.slice(0, 2000)` in onChange to the RTS statement textarea. Added a character counter below the field that turns amber at ≥1900 chars, matching the SignCardDialog pattern. | Tech creating a manual maintenance record with RTS checked pastes a long 43.9 certification paragraph (2500 chars). Enters PIN. Hits Create. Backend error. Auth event gone. Fix: field capped at 2000 chars with live counter showing approach to limit. |

A parts clerk pasting a long OEM description or notes into the description field could exceed the backend schema limit and get a cryptic validation error on submit. For `notes`, a `<Textarea>` with no `maxLength` or `.slice()` guard — consistent with the pattern fixed in BUG-PC-082 and others, but this create form was missed. Part numbers and serial numbers are rendered in the loaner list, loan-out dialog item summary, and return dialog item summary — an overflow would break those layouts. | `app/(app)/parts/loaners/page.tsx` | Added `maxLength={50}` + `.slice(0, 50)` to `partNumber`. Added `maxLength={50}` + `.slice(0, 50)` to `serialNumber`. Added `maxLength={200}` + `.slice(0, 200)` to `description`. Added `maxLength={500}` + `.slice(0, 500)` to `notes` Textarea. | Parts clerk creates a loaner item for a specialty tool set. Pastes a long vendor description. Submit fails. Item not created. Fix: fields capped client-side, submit always succeeds. |
| BUG-PC-086 | **Shipping page was missing a "Cancelled" filter tab.** `STATUS_TABS` defined All, Pending, In Transit, Delivered — but the `cancelled` status is a valid shipment state returned by the API (used by the Cancel button on every active shipment). The `counts` memo also didn't compute cancelled count. A parts clerk tracking which inbound shipments were cancelled (to follow up on re-orders) had to scroll through the "All" tab — which includes delivered and in-transit shipments — to find cancelled ones. With high shipment volume this is impossible to manage. | `app/(app)/parts/shipping/page.tsx` | Added `cancelled` to `counts` memo. Added `<TabsTrigger value="cancelled">Cancelled</TabsTrigger>` to the filter tab row. | Parts clerk needs to see all cancelled inbound shipments to verify which were re-ordered. No Cancelled tab forces manual scroll through all shipments. Fix: one-click filter to cancelled shipments. |
| BUG-PC-087 | **Rotables "Create" button had no loading/disabled state, allowing double-submits.** `handleCreate` called `createRotable()` with no `isCreatingRotable` state tracking — the button was always enabled and the dialog could be dismissed mid-submit. A parts clerk on a slow connection who double-clicks "Create" would fire two concurrent `createRotable` mutations, potentially creating duplicate rotable records for the same serial number. Rotable serial numbers should be unique — a duplicate would corrupt the lifecycle tracking. Also added dialog close guard to prevent escape-key dismissal mid-submission. | `app/(app)/parts/rotables/page.tsx` | Added `isCreatingRotable` state. Added `setIsCreatingRotable(true/false)` in `handleCreate` try/finally. Added `disabled={isCreatingRotable}` + Loader2 spinner to submit button. Added `if (isCreatingRotable) return` guard to dialog `onOpenChange`. | Parts clerk creating a $15,000 APU on slow airport WiFi double-clicks Create. Two rotable records created for same S/N. Lifecycle tracking is split across two records — one gets all history, the other is empty but shows in the list. Fix: button disabled during submit, dialog locked during mutation. |
| BUG-PC-088 | **`parts/new/page.tsx` `receivingDate` and `certSignatureDate` defaults used UTC date (`new Date().toISOString().slice(0, 10)`).** Same class as BUG-QCM-REC-001 and BUG-LT-HUNT-077 — UTC date string shows tomorrow's date for shops in UTC-negative timezones working late. A parts clerk in UTC-5 receiving parts at 9pm local (= 02:00 UTC next day) would see tomorrow's date pre-filled in both the Receiving Date and the 8130-3 Signature Date fields. A parts receiving record or 8130-3 with the wrong date is a compliance issue — it won't match the paper 8130-3 in hand or the PO receiving timestamp. The reset calls after successful submit had the same bug. | `app/(app)/parts/new/page.tsx` | Changed `useState<string>(new Date().toISOString().slice(0, 10))` to lazy initializer `useState<string>(() => { const d = new Date(); ... })` using local year/month/day components for both `receivingDate` and `certSignatureDate`. Fixed both post-submit reset calls to use the same local date pattern. | UTC-5 parts clerk receives a part at 8pm local. System pre-fills "March 4" for receiving date. Paper 8130-3 says "March 3". Record doesn't match document. Compliance flag. Fix: date always reflects clerk's local calendar date. |
| BUG-BM-089 | **New Quote page had no "Valid Until" (expiresAt) field.** `createQuote` accepts an optional `expiresAt` timestamp but the New Quote form had no corresponding input. Quotes were always created with no expiry date — violating standard MRO practice where a quote is only valid for a specific period (parts prices and labor rates are volatile). The quote detail page supports editing the expiry date after creation, but billing managers would have to remember to set it in a second step every time, or leave quotes perpetually valid. A customer could accept a 6-month-old quote with outdated pricing and the system would have no mechanism to flag it. | `app/(app)/billing/quotes/new/page.tsx` | Added `expiresAt` state with a lazy initializer defaulting to today + 30 days (industry standard). Added a "Valid Until" date input to the Quote Details card above Notes. Wired `expiresAt` into the `createQuote` mutation call. | Billing manager creates a quote for a $30,000 engine inspection. Pricing is good for 30 days. Customer comes back 90 days later. Without expiry date, system shows the quote as still valid. Billing manager accepts at stale pricing — loses money on parts. Fix: valid-until field always set at creation, defaults to +30 days. |
| BUG-BM-090 | **Time Approval page had no per-technician filter.** The Time Clock page (which billing managers also use) has a technician dropdown filter and text search. Time Approval only had a "Context" filter (All / Shop / Work Order / Task / Step). In a shop with 10–15 techs submitting time, a billing manager doing targeted review ("approve all of Jake's time from yesterday") had to scroll through every pending entry to find Jake's work — context filter doesn't help here. The bulk "Approve All" button would also approve ALL pending entries instead of just Jake's. | `app/(app)/billing/time-approval/page.tsx` | Added `techFilter` state (default `"all"`). Added `applyTechFilter()` helper that filters entries by `technicianId`. Applied to `filteredPending`, `filteredApproved`, and `filteredRejected` memos (stacked with existing `applyContextFilter`). Added "Technician" `<Select>` dropdown to the header filter bar populated from the `technicians` query. `bulkApproveEntries` naturally uses `filteredPending` which now respects the tech filter. | Billing manager reviewing a 25-entry queue wants to approve all of Jake's 8 entries. With no tech filter, has to click approve 8 times on specific rows while scrolling past 17 others. Can't use "Approve All" safely. Fix: select Jake from dropdown → queue shows his 8 entries → "Approve All (8)" does exactly what's expected. |
| BUG-BM-091 | **New Quote "Notes" textarea had no `maxLength` cap.** A billing manager pasting a long scope-of-work description or legal terms paragraph into the Notes field could exceed the backend schema limit and get a cryptic validation error after filling out all other fields and line items. All other notes/textarea fields across the app have been capped (BUG-LT-HUNT-054, BUG-QCM-C1, BUG-LT-HUNT-080, etc.) but the New Quote notes was missed. The field also had no character counter to signal proximity to the limit. | `app/(app)/billing/quotes/new/page.tsx` | Added `maxLength={1000}` and `.slice(0, 1000)` onChange to the Notes textarea. Added a `{notes.length}/1000` character counter below the field. | Billing manager pastes a full scope-of-work paragraph from the customer's RFQ email (1400 chars) into Notes. Adds 8 line items. Clicks Create. Backend error. All line items lost. Has to redo from scratch with truncated notes. Fix: field caps at 1000 chars client-side, counter shows approach to limit. |
| BUG-BM-092 | **Deposits page missing `toast` import and success/error feedback for Record Deposit and Apply Deposit actions.** Both dialogs closed silently on success — no toast, no visual confirmation. A billing manager recording a $5,000 deposit by check from a customer would submit, dialog closes, and nothing happens visibly until the table re-fetches. On slow connections or a second click, they might re-submit the same deposit. Apply Deposit had the same issue — manager applies $2,500 of a deposit to an invoice, dialog closes, no confirmation. Table eventually updates but there's a confusing moment of "did it work?" | `app/(app)/billing/deposits/page.tsx` | Added `import { toast } from "sonner"`. Added `toast.success(\`Deposit of ${fmt(amtNum)} recorded.\`)` in `RecordDepositDialog.handleSubmit` after successful mutation. Added `toast.success(\`${fmt(amtNum)} deposit applied to invoice.\`)` in `ApplyDepositDialog.handleSubmit` after successful mutation. | Billing manager records a $10k wire deposit. Dialog closes. Table shows loading. No toast. She calls the front desk to confirm it went through. Fix: toast confirms amount and action immediately. |
| BUG-BM-093 | **Credit Memos `ApplyCreditMemoDialog.handleApply` missing success toast.** The "Create Credit Memo" flow already had a `toast.success("Credit memo issued")`, but the Apply action (linking a credit memo to an invoice) closed silently with no feedback. A billing manager applying a $500 credit to Invoice #INV-0042 gets a dialog close with zero confirmation that the credit was applied, the invoice balance was reduced, or the credit memo status changed to APPLIED. | `app/(app)/billing/credit-memos/page.tsx` | Added `toast.success("Credit memo applied to invoice.")` in `ApplyCreditMemoDialog.handleApply` after the `await apply(...)` mutation succeeds. | Billing manager applies a credit. Nothing happens visually. Clicks Apply again. Tries to apply the same credit memo twice. Second attempt throws a backend error. Fix: success toast on first apply confirms the action completed. |
| BUG-BM-094 | **Credit Memos `isLoading` guard excluded `invoices === undefined`.** `isLoading = !isLoaded \|\| creditMemos === undefined \|\| customers === undefined` — invoices were loaded but not included in the guard. The `CreateCreditMemoDialog` `eligibleInvoices` memo and the `ApplyCreditMemoDialog` `eligibleInvoices` memo both receive `invoices ?? []`. If `invoices` was still undefined when the page finished its skeleton state (customers and credit memos loaded first), clicking "New Credit Memo" or "Apply" would open a dialog showing "No eligible invoices" — even though invoices exist. Same pattern fixed on the Deposits page simultaneously. | `app/(app)/billing/credit-memos/page.tsx` + `app/(app)/billing/deposits/page.tsx` | Added `\|\| invoices === undefined` to both `isLoading` expressions. Skeleton persists until invoices have loaded, so dialogs always open with the correct invoice list. | Billing manager opens Credit Memos on a fast org with 20 invoices. Customers load in 50ms, invoices in 200ms. Clicks "New Credit Memo" at 100ms. Invoice dropdown shows empty. Thinks no invoices are eligible. Creates credit memo without linking it. Has to re-open and apply it manually. Fix: dialog only opens after invoices are ready. |
| BUG-BM-095 | **Recurring Templates "Next Generate Date" input had no `min` date constraint or past-date validation.** The date picker accepted any date, including past dates. A billing manager accidentally setting the next generate date to January 2025 (months in the past) would create a template with an immediately-overdue trigger date — potentially generating a batch of invoices at the next scheduled run, or presenting as a data anomaly in the recurring jobs queue. No server-side date guard existed in the form. | `app/(app)/billing/recurring/page.tsx` | Added `min={new Date().toISOString().split("T")[0]}` to the "Next Generate Date" `<Input>` — browser prevents past-date selection via native date picker. Added `if (new Date(nextGenerateAt).getTime() < Date.now() - 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000)` guard in `handleSubmit` with `toast.error("Next generate date must be today or in the future.")` for defense-in-depth against manual entry. | Billing manager setting up a recurring monthly labor contract for a new customer accidentally enters last month's date in the "Next Generate" field (copy-paste from a reference). Template saved with a past trigger. Background job picks it up and fires immediately. Customer receives an invoice before the contract start date. Fix: native picker limits to today+, submit guard catches manual entries. |
| BUG-BM-096 | **Invoice Detail page had no "Add Line Item" button for DRAFT invoices.** `api.billing.addInvoiceLineItem` mutation exists on the backend (enforces DRAFT-only gate) but was never wired into the UI. The backend mutation accepts type (labor/part/external_service), description, qty, and unitPrice. | `app/(app)/billing/invoices/[id]/page.tsx` | Added `addInvoiceLineItem` mutation hook, `addLineDialog` state, and `handleAddLine` handler. Realizes they forgot to include a $150 consumables charge. With no Add Line button, they have to void and recreate the entire invoice. Fix: "Add Line" button opens dialog → billing manager adds "Consumables" labor at $150 → invoice total updates immediately. |
| BUG-BM-097 | **Warranty page had no search bar.** With 8 status tabs but zero text search, a billing manager tracking down a specific warranty claim by claim number, part number, or description had to scroll through the full list filtered only by status. In a shop with 50+ warranty claims, finding "the cracked gear box claim from last October" requires reading every row. The `claims` query returns the full dataset client-side; filtering locally is cheap and already the pattern across all other billing list pages. | `app/(app)/billing/warranty/page.tsx` | Added `search` state and a `claimRows` `useMemo` that filters by `claimNumber`, `partNumber`, `serialNumber`, and `description` (case-insensitive). | BUG-BM-098 | **Analytics page "Top 5 Customers by Quote Value" table rows were not clickable/linked.** Customer names appeared as plain text — a billing manager who sees "Coastal Air Charter" with $120k in quotes has no way to drill down to that customer's invoices, payments, or account history without manually navigating to the Customers section and searching. ## Bug Hunter Fixes — Shop Manager Cycle 88 (2026-03-03T17:43Z)

| ID | What Was Broken | File | What Changed | Why It Matters to the User |
|----|----------------|------|--------------|---------------------------|
| BUG-SM-102 | **Dashboard "Parts Awaiting Inspection" KPI card linked to `/parts/requests` (disposition queue) instead of `/parts/receiving` (receiving inspection queue).** The query correctly fetches `location: "pending_inspection"` parts — these are parts that have arrived in the shop and are waiting for a receiving inspection (8130-3 verification, condition check, etc.). The click-through went to `/parts/requests` which is the parts disposition/requisition queue — a completely different workflow. A shop manager clicking the red "3 Parts Awaiting Inspection" badge would land on the wrong page and see no connection to what the KPI was tracking. | `app/(app)/dashboard/page.tsx` | Changed `href: "/parts/requests"` to `href: "/parts/receiving"` in the `LiveSecondaryKPIs` "Parts Awaiting Inspection" card. | Shop manager sees "2 Parts Awaiting Inspection" alert on the dashboard. Clicks it. Old: lands on Parts Requests page (wrong). Searches around, gives up. Fix: clicking navigates directly to Parts Receiving where the pending items are listed. |
| BUG-SM-103 | **Reports Overview Revenue Summary Table used `.toLocaleString()` without `minimumFractionDigits: 2`, silently dropping cents.** JavaScript's default `toLocaleString()` strips trailing fractional zeros — `(1234.50).toLocaleString()` → `"1,234.5"` (not `"1,234.50"`). The Revenue column, per-row revenue cells, and the Total row footer all had this defect. In an MRO context, billing amounts are frequently non-round (labor at $95/hr, parts markups, freight). A revenue report showing "$4,218.5" vs "$4,218.50" looks like broken formatting to a billing-aware shop manager and erodes trust in the reports. | `app/(app)/reports/page.tsx` | Changed all three `$${value.toLocaleString()}` instances to `$${value.toLocaleString("en-US", { minimumFractionDigits: 2, maximumFractionDigits: 2 })}` — summary paragraph total, per-row cell, and the Total footer row. | Shop manager checks the revenue report for last quarter. Sees "$82,414.5" in the Total column. Thinks the system dropped a digit. Calls billing to verify. Fix: "$82,414.50" — standard two-decimal money formatting, consistent with the Financial Dashboard. |
| BUG-SM-104 | **Schedule Health Widget "+X more" overflow text was non-clickable plain text.** When more than 4 at-risk WOs existed, the widget showed "+3 more" as a `<p>` tag with no link. The overflow count creates expectation that it's clickable (like a pagination link). | `app/(app)/dashboard/_components/ScheduleHealthWidget.tsx` | Replaced `<p>+{count} more</p>` with `<Link to="/work-orders">+{count} more — View all in Work Orders →</Link>` using `text-primary hover:underline` styling. | Shop manager sees "Schedule Health — 6 need attention".
